  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a0281cfb-df90-4f5e-99d1-17e65535a928'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText4260223378775707208" style="display:none">Rise up while you can. -Georgia Mason<br /><br />The year was 2014. The year we cured cancer. The year we cured the common cold. And the year the dead started to walk. The year of the Rising.<br /><br />The year was 2039. The world didn't end when the zombies came, it just got worse. Georgia and Shaun Mason set out on the biggest story of their generation. They uncovered the biggest conspiracy since the Rising and realized that to tell the truth, sacrifices have to be made.<br /><br />Now, the year is 2041, and the investigation that began with the election of President Ryman is much bigger than anyone had assumed. With too much left to do and not much time left to do it in, the surviving staff of After the End Times must face mad scientists, zombie bears, rogue government agencies-and if there's one thing they know is true in post-zombie America, it's this:<br /><br />Things can always get worse.<br /><br /><i>Blackout</i> is the conclusion to the epic trilogy that began in the Hugo-nominated <i>Feed</i> and the sequel, <i>Deadline</i>.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/228926-okaaay-when-beck-and-shaun-sleep">Okaaay. When Beck and Shaun sleep together, why did Beck got hurt the next morning? I know Shaun said George&#39;s name but kindle explain to me in laymans term please?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_228926'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F11806716-blackout">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/228926-okaaay-when-beck-and-shaun-sleep">See all 4 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/8181405-lisa"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442964476i/8181405._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/8181405-lisa">Lisa</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    When Becks tells the Monkey (the forger) her last love interest was an incestuous necrophilac, she's referring to Shaun, who after immediately having <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    When Becks tells the Monkey (the forger) her last love interest was an incestuous necrophilac, she's referring to Shaun, who after immediately having sex with Becks, refers to her as George (the deceased, adoptive sister he still talks to, and imagines seeing and touching). Apparently, he'd imagined he was making love with George, not Becks. So, not only did Shaun not requite Becks' feelings for him, Becks felt used, as she felt Shaun had had sex with her merely as a proxy for making love with his true, dead sweetheart, who Becks would never be able to compete with.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=get-the-scoop">get-the-scoop</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350104240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14489557393733626791">Here’s a book called <i>Blackout</i> that seems hugely popular with critics and the Goodreads crowd, but that I thought had serious flaws despite a cool premise. Now I’ve written a long review going in depth into what irritated me so much. Hmm… I wonder why I’ve got this odd feeling of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127181517' rel='nofollow noopener'>deja vu</a>?<br/><br/>This is the third book in the Newsflesh trilogy after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160642555' rel='nofollow noopener'>Feed</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193673289' rel='nofollow noopener'>Deadline</a> in which Mira Grant* created a future world set about twenty-five years after mutated viruses created zombies. In this future, where dying b</span>
  <span id="freeText14489557393733626791" style="display:none">Here’s a book called <i>Blackout</i> that seems hugely popular with critics and the Goodreads crowd, but that I thought had serious flaws despite a cool premise. Now I’ve written a long review going in depth into what irritated me so much. Hmm… I wonder why I’ve got this odd feeling of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127181517" rel="nofollow noopener">deja vu</a>?<br /><br />This is the third book in the Newsflesh trilogy after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160642555" rel="nofollow noopener">Feed</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193673289" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadline</a> in which Mira Grant* created a future world set about twenty-five years after mutated viruses created zombies. In this future, where dying by any means causes the dormant virus to go active and turn any corpse into a potential brain eater, large parts of the world have been ceded to the undead while the so-called safe zones are made up of fortified locations and rigid security measures. <br /><br /><i>* A pen name for Seanan McGuire.</i><br /><br />Bloggers have become the most trusted source of news since traditional media did nothing to inform people about the danger or what to do during the initial zombie uprising. The story revolves around some of these on-line journalists who got thrown in the middle of a vast political conspiracy that has cost them dearly.<br /><br />To find an example of one of my biggest problems with these books I need to look no further than the zombie bear in this one. In Grant’s version of the future, the large mammals like horses, cows and bigger dogs can also turn into zombies, and we get the potential for an awesome scene when a couple of the main characters run across a zombie bear while traveling, and they have no choice but to take it down. If you’re the kind of person who has dedicated a significant amount of time to reading over 1700 total pages of a zombie story, the idea of a fight with a zombie bear should fill you with glee and anticipation.<br /><br />What Grant does is some foreshadowing about the appearance of a zombie bear, then has the zombie bear show and get two characters all revved up to fight it. They grab their guns and jump out of their vehicle to take on this goddamn zombie bear, and then……<br /><br />She cuts to the next chapter where something else is going on. Later on we get a brief blog post from one of the characters saying that he killed a zombie bear and it was fun.<br /><br />This incident makes me pretty sure that Mira Grant isn’t from Missouri. You know, the SHOW-ME STATE. If there was one of the fifty that was a I'LL-STRONGLY-HINT-THAT-SOMETHING-AWESOME-IS-ABOUT-TO-HAPPEN-REPEATEDLY-BUT-NEVER-QUITE-PAY-IT-OFF STATE, that’s where Mira Grant would be from. (But that motto would probably be tough to fit on a license plate.)<br /><br />I gotta a lot of other problems with this book and the entire trilogy. In order to maximize my bitching, I’ve broken them into these categories that are spoiler free:<br /><br /><b>The Grant Repetition Principle</b> - Apparently Mira Grant thinks all of her readers have the same condition as Guy Pierce in <i>Memento</i> and that none of us are capable of producing short term memories because she repeats shit constantly to either remind us of things or reuse the same plot points, scenes or dialogue over and over again. If the Internet hasn’t completely devastated your attention span, this gets annoying in a hurry. This repetition causes the other issues I had with the book to become even more irritating because if she does something that annoys you once, you can bet it’s going to happen about fifty more times over the course of the three books.<br /><br /><b>Mira Grant Wants To Suck Your Blood!</b> - If I had a nickel for every blood screening that happens in these books, I could make Bill Gates my pool boy. Yes, this is a society locked down and living in fear because of a virus, but that doesn’t mean that the details of all those tests have to be repeated. Even worse is that Grant gets stuck on certain phrases and descriptions. The subject almost always “Slaps my palm on the panel.” and then they wince as “The needles bit into my skin.”<br /><br />First off, if it’s a blood test with needles, why would you ‘Slap my palm on the panel’? Why not “Place my palm gently on the panel.”?<br /><br />Secondly, I’ve got a cat with diabetes who has required two injections of insulin a day for five years or so. That means I’ve injected him over 3600 times. In all of those, I have never once ‘bit’ him with a needle. I’ve ‘jabbed’ him with a needle. I’ve ‘poked’ him with a needle. I’ve ‘pierced’ him with a needle. I’ve ‘stung’ him with a needle. But no ‘biting’.<br /><br />It’s called a thesaurus, Mira. Look into it. Or better yet, just cut down on the blood tests.<br /><br /><b>Have A Coke And A Smile</b> - I’m pretty sure that Coca-Cola must have paid some kind of product placement fee because there’s no other way to figure out why it seems like someone is drinking one on every other page. Since Mira is also assuming that none of us can remember what a Coke tastes like, she lets us know how sweet it is every time. <br /><br />Particularly bad was this exchange on page 511 which I think is Coke # 2465 in this book:<br /><br /><i>“How are you feeling?”<br /><br />“Exhausted. I need a Coke.”<br /><br />I was never going to get tired of hearing those words. </i><br /><br />That’s when I realized that Mira Grant has got to be fucking with us.<br /><br /><b>Where Are All The Zombies? And What Do They Look Like?</b> - <i>Blackout</i> has 632 pages. Of this, only about 40 actually feature any kind of encounters with zombies. That’s about 6% of the book, and that ratio is about the same for the other two. And whenever zombies do show up, there is an almost complete lack of description of them. They are just ‘zombies’. No mention of age, gender, clothing, state of decay or anything else. I know that giving detailed descriptions of zombie hordes would be impossible, but if you don’t describe at least a few of them, then it’s just this nebulous vague threat.<br /><br />Maybe if we could have had a few less blood tests and Cokes, there would have been time for some more zombie fightin’ action and maybe a couple of descriptions to let us know what they looked like.<br /><br /><b>Are You Threatening Me?</b> - Our heroes love to threaten people. They threaten both their enemies and friends constantly. Following the Grant Repetition Principle, most of these threats are pretty similar. Someone is always A) Going to get shot. Or B) Going to be punched in the face.<br /><br />These threats are doled out in conversation and in the blog posts that lead off every chapters, but don’t worry if you get told that you’re going to be punched or shot. These guys talk a good game, but they never really follow through on anything.<br /><br />In fact, they are given to make bold pronouncements of how they’re about to unleash hell on somebody. Never happens. Probably because they all appear to be manic depressives as illustrated in our next category.<br /><br /><b>Game Over, Man! Game Fucking Over!</b> - When not telling everyone how they’re gonna shoot them or punch them in the face, our heroes tend to get pessimistic. Once again, we can look to the Grant Repetition Principle to get countless instances of someone confidently asserting that they’re all going to die soon. It does not so much build up a state of fear and dread for their future as it bores the shit out me.<br /><br />Here are more categories with spoilers. I am giving up major plot points from all books as well as the ending of this one so do not read if you don’t want to know.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br /><b>Send In The Clones</b> - One of the strongest moments of the series was when our first person narrator George was deliberately infected with the virus which forced her brother Shaun to shoot and kill her as she made her final blog entry. That scene pushed <i>Feed</i> up several notches for me as well as making me think that Mira Grant may have some pretty bold tricks up her sleeve.<br /><br />Turns out the trick was to have a clone of George introduced in this one. That dropped my opinion of the entire story because now George’s ‘death’ was just emotional manipulation of the reader that had no true consequences. So there’s both a tragic death to let everyone break their hankies out, but still a happy ending to cheer.<br /><br />Bullshit. <br /><br /><b>Shaun Mason Is A Douche Bag</b> - I don’t know if Mira Grant has ever actually talked to any men or not, but if this is her view of what we’re like, then I feel like our entire gender has been insulted.<br /><br />As the daredevil Irwin who ‘pokes dead things with sticks’ (Yet another example of the Grant Repetition Principle), Shaun was just a loyal but brainless minion to George in the first book. George’s death could have forced him into being an interesting character in the second one. Instead what we got was a self-absorbed abusive fuck who would punch his own employees if they dared mention his sacred sister’s name in a way he disapproved of and who preferred to go crazy town banana pants rather than deal with the here and now.<br /><br />Fuck him. <br /><br />Oops, I didn’t mean literally, George!<br /><br /><b>Incest!</b> - I gather there’s a bit of controversy about the whole thing of George and Shaun being lovers. Since it was well established that they were adopted and not related by blood, then I didn’t have a problem with it.<br /><br />What I did think was beyond creepy was that they continued to refer to each other as brother and sister rather than girlfriend, boyfriend, lover, sweet patootie, etc. <br /><br />Yeah, I know George’s bullshit explanation about how they had to keep it secret because of their public image. Uh…No. Have a press conference and explain that you fell in love with the person you’ve known and trusted longer than anyone and stress that you are not actually related. Most people would probably be cool with that, but if they find out you’re secretly sleeping with someone you still refer to as your brother?<br /><br />Yuck.<br /><br /><b>The Romeo And Juliet Factor</b> - So George was dead for a while and it made Shaun into an asshole as well as crazy. We’re told over and over (The GRP again.) how he was always meant to outlive George, and how when he finally settles up with the vast conspiracy, he’s going to go off and just live with Ghost George in his head and be completely shit-your-pants-crazy. When George comes back from the dead, she mentions several times that they always thought that Shaun would die first, and after he did, she would bury him and then kill herself.<br /><br />Obsessive, unhealthy love affairs that end in madness and/or suicide are not what I’m looking for in my zombie books.<br /><br /><b>The CDC Needs New Locks</b> - In <i>Deadline</i> Shaun and company make two long and dangerous journeys to confront the CDC in two different cities. Both times end in disaster. In this one, they actually have a plan that makes some sense, but have to turn around and come back to Seattle before completing any of it. <br /><br />And then they break into the CDC again.<br /><br />Seriously, Mira?<br /><br /><b>The Stupidest Conspiracy Story Since The X-Files Went Off The Air</b> - So the evil CDC was controlling the President by holding his wife and kids hostage while giving him a clone wife for the cameras. George was cloned by the CDC so that a programmed version could be used to manipulate and betray Shaun, but the underground elements led by the Vice-President used that to get a ‘good’ George and break the story about the virus to the world. Because George’s credibility is so fucking awesome that even showing up after being dead in a world full of blood thirsty zombies, people would instantly believe her.<br /><br />The first stage of the plan? Have the president’s family freed in ten minutes by using secret elements the good guys already had in position.(Another action that we’re only told about, but don‘t get any details on.) George gets a gun and goes to the room with the Prez and evil CDC guy, tells everyone that the jig is up and then a Secret Sevice guy kills the CDC dude. After escaping the zombie outbreak, the files get sent out by their news site and George does a video telling everyone to listen to the President who tells everyone what’s been going on.<br /><br />Sooooooooo…… Why exactly were George and Shaun so important again? Supposedly their credibility was vital to the plans of both sides. Maybe if instead of fucking around for over a year while trying to clone George, the VP and the loyal Secret Service agents could have just freed the President’s family, which apparently could have happened at any time since it was so easy that it was done in ten minutes after one phone call, and then just put him on TV to say that the CDC is EEEEVVVIIIIIIILLLLLL! <br /><br />No one would have listened to the goddamn President of the United States if he said that his family was held hostage by the CDC? The only person that anyone in the world will believe is Georgia Mason? Christ, if people are that cynical in 2040 than just go ahead and clone Walter Cronkite to break the news. <br /><br />I guess that wouldn’t work because….<br /><br /><b>George &amp; Shaun Mason Are The Only People That Matter In The World!</b> - Yeah, there’s some lip service paid to other people on their team, but by shifting the first person narration between two people who really only care about each other, it makes the books completely about them. <br /><br />And if you’re trying to create a story that involves a vast political conspiracy and a worldwide plague of zombies, the scope needs to be wider than two people utterly obsessed with each other. <br /><br />Part of the reason that I don’t buy the idea that George is the only journalist in the world who will be believed is that we never once saw what kind of impact her writing had. Yes, we were once again told how it got the President elected and all that, and they sometimes talked about their high ratings in <i>Feed</i>, but we never got a viewpoint from anyone else as to what their reporting meant to anyone reading it.<br /><br />Over the course of these books, Oakland got firebombed and Florida was supposedly lost to hurricanes and zombie mosquitoes, and yet all of it was told to us third hand. Somewhere in these 1700 pages there should have been room to let us know what people outside of the George &amp; Shaun bubble thought was going on.<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I’ve spent so much time breaking this down because these three books ended up seeming like a wasted opportunity to me. Mira Grant came up with an intriguing twist on the zombie genre. Despite the flaws, she’s also got a compulsively readable style at times. When she remembered that she was writing a zombie novel and threw in some action, she actually did a pretty good job of it. There’s two tense and action filled conflicts with the undead in this that are top notch, but as I’ve pointed out here, that made up a very small portion of the overall story.<br /><br />Instead of delivering on the potential of the world she created, she focused instead on the inner lives and emotional state of a couple of characters that became boring and irritating when she couldn’t think of enough stuff for them to do and just repeated the same crap over and over again.<br /><br />Here endth the rant.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14489557393733626791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_167342263" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167342263" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167342263?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic-utopian">dystopian-post-apocalyptic-utopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=june">june</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=asian">asian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=crush-worthy-boys">crush-worthy-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-zombies-biters">pn-zombies-biters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2012-publication">2012-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167342263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3239713511332737036"><b>This review is spoiler-free, and safe even for those who haven't read the first two books in the series.</b><br/><br/>Forget everything you ever assumed about science fiction novels or zombie thrillers: the Newsflesh trilogy defies all expectations. The story that began with a turbulent political campaign in a post-apocalyptic <i>Feed</i> escalates here as the blogger journalists from After the End of Times continue their quest to uncover the truth behind the deadly Kellis-Amberlee virus that has decimated civilizat</span>
  <span id="freeText3239713511332737036" style="display:none"><b>This review is spoiler-free, and safe even for those who haven't read the first two books in the series.</b><br /><br />Forget everything you ever assumed about science fiction novels or zombie thrillers: the Newsflesh trilogy defies all expectations. The story that began with a turbulent political campaign in a post-apocalyptic <i>Feed</i> escalates here as the blogger journalists from After the End of Times continue their quest to uncover the truth behind the deadly Kellis-Amberlee virus that has decimated civilization--one that is now mutating and spreading faster than ever before. The breakneck action and intrigue in <i>Blackout</i> is intense as a dangerous rescue mission, disease-carrying mosquitoes, zombie bears, tangled family drama, and a mysterious patient known as Subject 7B all complicate what is already hell on earth.<br /><br />It's funny that my favorite zombie series actually has the least amount of zombie action in it, but Newsflesh hasn't ever been about the undead anyway--it's about the human response to it. As with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166678103" rel="nofollow noopener">The Reapers Are the Angels</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170440313" rel="nofollow noopener">Warm Bodies</a>, this series is fascinating to me because it explores the idea of personal integrity within extreme circumstances. What would you do when the world ends? If you're Shaun and Georgia Mason, adopted siblings whose closeness forms an unbreakable team, you lead your fellow bloggers into an unrelenting search for truth--no matter what the cost. Or at least, that's how their story began. But now that the stakes are higher than they've ever been and those they love most are at risk, the focus has shifted to a very human need to hold onto the connections that matter most.<br /><br /><b><i>Blackout</i> seamlessly combines medical thriller, political intrigue, and pulse-pounding action sequences with unforgettable human drama.</b> How you feel about this series will very much depend on how you feel about the characters in general--if you love the Masons, Alaric, Becks, Mahir, and Maggie, you'll most likely have a fantastic time with Newsflesh. It doesn't mean the characters are perfect, of course; Shaun in particular is mourning a huge loss, and his reckless, desperate behavior in the second book caused a lot of criticism from a lot of readers. For me, I felt his pain so keenly, however, that his torment became mine--and I understood, too, the unconventional, defiant ways in which he grasped for some semblance of happiness as the world around him was destroyed. In books and in real life, I respond very strongly to loyalty, honesty, and the determination to do what's right. Shaun and Georgia, as well as their superbly realized supporting cast, embody those traits in a big way. Because they also are slammed with unbelievable suffering throughout these books that require a brutal amount of self-sacrifice, it isn't any wonder that I feel such fiercely protective love for them, as well as for the ideals they represent. <br /><br />The author's writing gets better and better in each book, with well-researched scientific dilemmas and brilliant recaps that engage the reader without resorting to long info-dumps. Her brisk, matter-of-fact style of writing suits the story perfectly, and the sophisticated plot is exceptionally well-paced, with shifts from furious action to moments of stark stillness and contemplation handled beautifully. Whether we're getting worked up over red herrings, watching someone facing her own mortality, or respectfully acknowledging fallen comrades, the emotional pitch throughout the book felt utterly right, which is something that is very hard to pull off when there are so many ethical issues at stake.<br /><br /><b>A few random thoughts with REAL spoilers</b>, because there's no other way to discuss them:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Subject 7B's realization of who and what she is is totally kickass. I loved how very true to her character this whole scenario was, and how believably all the cloning issues were integrated with our human need to recognize this person.<br /><br />The scenes where 7B looks on the 8s made me really sad. :(<br /><br />I'm so glad that one of the major plot points wasn't rescuing Georgia, because I cannot imagine any situation less likely to happen. The way she escapes and the way everyone reacts to seeing her was pitch-perfect.<br /><br />I am SO happy to have Georgia back. Sheesh, I missed her so much! And it's nice to have a break from all the crazy of being in Shaun's head, hah.<br /><br />I'm glad that Shaun and Georgia got to ride off into the sunset a bit, though I'm still sad for the brave, original Georgia who died in such a devastating way.<br /><br />There were certainly some plot lines that I saw coming, and although I'm a little surprised that we got a HEA, obviously this didn't hinder my enjoyment of the book at all. The way it was handled felt just right.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I don't know that I've ever read another series where the emotion it evoked was so intense--<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165644673" rel="nofollow noopener">Feed</a> left me crying so hard I could hardly see the keyboard, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167342264" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadline</a> had me literally whimpering with pain in the middle of the night, and <i>Blackout</i> made me want to scream with excitement and agony and worry all at once. If you'd told me that a science fiction trilogy with zombies could be so searingly emotional or feel so incredibly personal, I'd have told you it was impossible. And I've never been happier to be proven wrong. I know most true fans of this series will race through the pages just like I did, with the same urgency and dread and excitement. <br /><br />While I'm so sad that this particular story is over (although there are two more Newsflesh novellas coming this year) and I dearly wish they could all turn into zombies so this story could live on forever, I'm happy with the way the story ended. I'm sure Mira Grant's new forthcoming novels <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13641105.Parasitology" title="Parasitology by Mira Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Parasitology</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13641108.Symbiogenesis" title="Symbiogenesis by Mira Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Symbiogenesis</a> will be absolutely spectacular. <br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2012/05/blackout-newsflesh-3-by-mira-grant-this.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher.</i><br /><br />P.S. For more proof of the power of Mira Grant's writing, <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2012/05/blackout-newsflesh-3-by-mira-grant-this.html" rel="nofollow noopener">read the alternate ending to FEED</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13793128.Fed" title="Fed by Mira Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Fed</a>, at the bottom of the review on our blog which is ONLY safe for those who have already read the first book. Holy frak, that woman is an evil genius.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3239713511332737036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review167342263">
  <td colspan="2">
    <div class="updateActionLinks">
        <a class="right flag" rel="nofollow" id="flag_link167342263" title="Flag this review as inappropriate." href="/flagged/new?resource_id=167342263&amp;resource_type=Review&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F11806716-blackout">flag</a>

<div id="review_338855650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/338855650" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/338855650?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=zombies-r-bitey">zombies-r-bitey</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer338855650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4726595414674749361">more, please.<br/>i don't want it to be over.<br/><br/>review when i stop hyperventilating.<br/><br/>.......................................................................<br/><br/>so, yeah. the only way to review this book is to squee over it like a little girl. because it's the final book in a trilogy - whatever i write here isn't going to make anyone who hasn't read the first two run right out and buy it, because these books build - there is no way to only read the third book and feel like you have made a good decision. and i</span>
  <span id="freeText4726595414674749361" style="display:none">more, please.<br>i don't want it to be over.<br><br>review when i stop hyperventilating.<br><br>.......................................................................<br><br>so, yeah. the only way to review this book is to squee over it like a little girl. because it's the final book in a trilogy - whatever i write here isn't going to make anyone who hasn't read the first two run right out and buy it, because these books build - there is no way to only read the third book and feel like you have made a good decision. and if you <i>have</i> read the first two books, obviously you are going to read the third one, so my review isn't going to be what convinces you to find out how it all ends, right? <br><br>so - commence the squee...<br><br>and i will be very very careful to avoid spoilers.<br>because i would have murdered anyone who had dared spoil it for me. <br><br>i thought this was a perfect conclusion to a trilogy. sure, there were some moments when i rolled my eyes a little: shaun's endless witty remarks, becks' behavior towards you-know-who in some of the scenes was a little much, and ditto with the fox. but both of them redeemed themselves, and performed such wonderful heroic acts, that my heart swelled repeatedly. but as far as tying up loose ends and giving her characters believable endings and leaving the reader with complete satisfaction in the world of her creation.... an easy five stars. <br><br>mira grant is just so masterful. the blog-excerpt chapter-openers are some of the best examples of reader-manipulation i have ever seen. she has a perfect sense of <i>rallying</i> the reader, you know what i mean? emotionally, they run the gamut from humorous, poignant, cheesy (that poetry...), and just flat-out triumphant - they made me want to rise along with them. it's a neat trick she accomplished, and a great way to supply additional depth to her characters.<br><br>one of my favorites:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ kill me once, shame on you.<br>kill me twice, shame on me.<br>kill my brother? oh, it's on. and you are <i>not</i> going to enjoy it <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>because i shouldn't really like the george character. she is so...earnest and driven and honest and sincere, usually a character like that would make me feel queasy. and we all know what happens to characters who are too noble for their surroundings, right?<br><br>this is not a spoiler for this book, but for a very popular series by george r r martin, so stay away, nerds:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380379227i/735366.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>but george (not martin) is great, and i don't know what it is about her that rescues her from my eye-rolling, except that she is just perfectly written; she is not some cookie-cutter character standing in for "all that is good and right and just", she is beaten and defiant and oh, god karen - don't use that picture again... oh god, you are going to, aren't you??<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380379227i/735367.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg">.<br><br>yup, it can't be helped... <br><br>and add her to shaun, and oh my god. a terrific explosion of capable badassery that just never lets up.<br><br>i love every little thing about this book. the attention to detail, the science that sounds pretty terrifyingly plausible to me, the nuance to characters, the way everyone has their own damage and their own coping mechanisms... it just feels <i>right</i> , all of it. it feels like i am not really reading it, but that i am immersed in something. and that is rare for me, with reading. i love reading, i do it all the time, but it is rare for me to experience this level of envelopment in a story. i was <i>there</i>, man...<br><br>yeah, it's a zombie book - get over it, it is also a book about the indomitable human spirit. and it fucking kicks ass.<br><br>alariiiiiiiic!!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4726595414674749361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_227464496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227464496" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227464496?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=rereading-material">rereading-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=male-approved">male-approved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=beloved">beloved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=best-of">best-of</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227464496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17239399982774817717">[SAFE TO READ] And so the story ends.. <br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/mira-grant/review-blackout.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361899i/712936.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I've never missed some characters the way I miss these guys, and yeah - I <strong>already</strong> miss them like crazy.<br/><br/>You know what?... If you want to know how this all ends you’ll just have to read the story and find on your own. <i>What you’re reading now is my heart bleeding all over my keyboard, because this is how it feels letting this story go.</i><br/><br/>Damn you Mira Grant, for making me love your world as much as I do, for making me cry for a fictional story and some freaki</span>
  <span id="freeText17239399982774817717" style="display:none">[SAFE TO READ] And so the story ends.. <br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/mira-grant/review-blackout.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361899i/712936.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I've never missed some characters the way I miss these guys, and yeah - I <strong>already</strong> miss them like crazy.<br><br>You know what?... If you want to know how this all ends you’ll just have to read the story and find on your own. <i>What you’re reading now is my heart bleeding all over my keyboard, because this is how it feels letting this story go.</i><br><br>Damn you Mira Grant, for making me love your world as much as I do, for making me cry for a fictional story and some freaking amazing characters that don’t even exist, for making me read a zombie book when I don’t even like zombies. Damn you for being such an amazing writer!<br><br>I wish I’d know how to say goodbye, how to close the book with a smile on my lips and not to feel this ache in my heart, I wish there was more to this story .. I find it so hard to get closer to writing the last line about the Masons, so hard to think that I will never again enjoy new adventures with them, so hard not to wait for another book in the series to come out.. It’s all simply too hard even though I understand that at some point we had to get to an ending.<br><br><a href="http://orange-zombie.com/allforsaken/?p=312" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361899i/712937.jpg" alt="" width="473" height="252" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><blockquote>"<b>Anyone coming within a hundred yards of my happy ending had better pray that they’re immune to bullets</b>" <br>~ Shaun Mason</blockquote><br>In terms of concept and world building, this story doesn’t add much to the awesomeness of the series. I think that all the mind-blowing details about this world have been squeezed into <a title="Review: Deadline" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/mira-grant/deadline-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadline</a> and <a title="Review: Feed" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/mira-grant/feed-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Feed</a>.<br>This is just how the story ends. This is how all the pieces are put together and the characters get to the point of really knowing the truth and deciding what to do with it. It is not a perfect ending, it is not a <em>happily ever after</em> for everyone, it still holds some questions and uncertainty, but it is as close to perfect as it can get to be.<br><br>I don't know if I am sad that it is really over, or if I am sad because of the way it all ended. I wanted more time with them, one more chapter, one more scene, one more joke, <strong>one more zombie to poke with a stick</strong>.<br><br><a href="http://orange-zombie.com/allforsaken/?attachment_id=53" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361899i/712938.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I am not sure if you've ever been in love with the characters in a story.. Like really loving them all, like never getting enough of them and wanting at least one more scene with them and missing them like crazy after you've turned the last page of the book.<br>I don't know if you usually cry when a dear character dies, or if you do it on special occasions like I do, but damn, how I hated every time one of my beloved book-character-friends had passed away, how I wanted to turn back the page and rewrite their ending, how they still haunt my memory and I remember them being so awesome and so funny, and brave, and (oh!) how I’ll miss them every time I’ll thing about this story.<br><br>My heart aches.. I am sitting here with my iPad on my lap, trying to say all the things that have been left unspoken, but I can't seem to find the right words.<br>This review was supposed to be full of spoilers, because I tried so much to hold back so many things about our character in the first 2 books that I deserved to let it all out at the very ending.. But I won’t because there's nothing I could possibly say that could match the awesomeness of this story, and telling you about how great these characters are won’t ever be enough.<br><br>Don't be fooled by the star (half star) missing from my rating though.. This story is as amazing as the whole series is; only Blackout is my least favorite of the 3 of them (a bit less funny, with not as much action, but tying nicely all the loose ends and giving these characters what they deserve).<br>I started reading it late in the evening, I didn't stop all night and I finished it after only 3 hours of sleep in the morning.. Maybe that's why my review notes didn't make much sense when I read them.<br><br>So, this is my goodbye for them.. And there’s nothing else I could say, other than the fact that I will really, really.. really miss them all.<br><br>I will miss the crazy cute <strong>Shaun</strong>, who used to think only about another stupid way to poke the dead with a stick for the ratings and who could make me laugh like crazy. I will miss his craziness and the way he could love with all his heart.<br><br><a href="http://s4.photobucket.com/albums/y126/VespertineFlora/Anime/#!cpZZ3QQtppZZ24" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361899i/712939.jpg" alt="" width="284" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I will miss <b>Georgia</b> and her devotion for unraveling the truth, I will miss her black-or-white point of view, I will miss the way she was so sure that she will be the one burying her brother.<br><br>I will, miss <b>Becks</b> and her sarcasm, the way she enjoyed being an Irwin, the way she wanted a solid proof before believing something. (and I’ll always think of her when I’ll drink a beer with her name on it)<br><br>I will miss <b>Mahir</b>, <b>Maggie</b>, and <b>Alaric</b>, how supportive they’ve been, how devoted to the Masons and their mission, how they’ve risked their lives so many times for the truth to come out, for being there for Shaun when he was going crazy, for supporting him even when he did stupid things, for missing Georgia and for being (together) the best bloggers in the zombie world.<br><br>And I will miss <strong>Buffy</strong> and <strong>Dave</strong> and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[all the other people that have died protecting the truth or trying to get it out, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I will miss every single character in the story, even some unrealistic evil characters with their annoying way of telling their 'master plan' before dying.<br><br><b>Goodbye, my dears!</b><br><br><br><br><br><b>CONCLUSION:</b><br>I will probably get to read other books by Mira Grant/ Seanan McGuire, but I will always miss this story in a way I’d never missed another one before.<br><br><br><br><br><b>One favorite quote from the many:</b><br><i>Because we chose to tell the truth<br>(The cool of age, the rage of youth)<br>And stand against the lies of old<br>(The whispers soft, the tales untold)<br>We find ourselves the walking dead<br>(The loves unkept, the words unsaid)<br>And in the crypt of all we've known<br>(The broken blade, the breaking stone)<br>We know that we were in the right<br>(The coming dawn, the ending night).<br>So here is when we stop the lies.<br>The time is come. We have to Rise.</i><br><br><i>~From Dandelion Mine, the blog of Magdalene Grace Garcia, August 7, 2041.</i><br><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/mira-grant/review-blackout.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/mira-grant/review-blackout.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><br><b>Pre-reading thoughts:</b><br><i>Well if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/8980373" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> didn't make an impression on you, I might need to try plan B:<br><a href="http://readingaftermidnight.s3.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/10/Pretty-pretty-please.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361899i/712940._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="450" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>Come on!.. I could be turned into a zombie in a year, we don't want <i>that</i> to happen, right? :D</i></i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_173457185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173457185" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173457185?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=amazing-writing">amazing-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=books-that-changed-me">books-that-changed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=my-flat-army">my-flat-army</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=role-models">role-models</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=highly-anticipating-2012">highly-anticipating-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2012">arc-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173457185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12795285213460556263">Worry not, my dears, this review is spoiler-free.<br/><br/><b><i>There are three things in this world I truly believe in. That the truth will set us free; that lies are the prisons we build for ourselves; and that Shaun loves me. Everything else is just details.</i><br/>- Georgia Mason</b><br/><br/>There's not much I can say about the Newsflesh trilogy that I haven't said a million times before, nothing spoiler-free at least, and I refuse to spoil even the smallest detail for any of you. As a result, this will be more of an emotional</span>
  <span id="freeText12795285213460556263" style="display:none">Worry not, my dears, this review is spoiler-free.<br /><br /><b><i>There are three things in this world I truly believe in. That the truth will set us free; that lies are the prisons we build for ourselves; and that Shaun loves me. Everything else is just details.</i><br />- Georgia Mason</b><br /><br />There's not much I can say about the Newsflesh trilogy that I haven't said a million times before, nothing spoiler-free at least, and I refuse to spoil even the smallest detail for any of you. As a result, this will be more of an emotional outburst than an actual review, so feel free to abandon ship if you’re not a fan of my all-too-frequent displays of sentimentality. I apologize in advance. <br /><br />How do you bring down a massive government conspiracy? You don’t. You do what the crew of After the End Times does: you run for your life, save a few people, bury more than a few, tell the truth, and make sure to get it all on camera. Oh, and you pay attention when the villain starts explaining his actions because there might me more to it than he’s ready to admit. And when you stop to think about it and realize that it’s not worth it at all, you keep doing it because there’s nothing else you <i>can</i> do, and you hope for the best. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>I didn’t dream of funerals this time. Instead, I dreamed of me and Shaun, walking hand in hand through the empty hall where the Republican National Convention was held, and nothing was trying to kill us. Nothing was trying to kill us at all.</i>
</b><br /><br />As the story progressed and the science in it became more and more wild, I kept expecting to reach the point where I’d stop believing it, where it would be too much, but I never did. Therein lies the talent of Seanan McGuire – she is able to make the craziest things sound entirely convincing. It helps that her sense of pacing is nothing short of extraordinary, not to mention her ability to emotionally manipulate her readers. It’s not easy to keep people engaged and utterly fascinated through more than 500 pages, and yet Seanan McGuire accomplished it no less than three times. <br /><br />I could (and should) say that the Newsflesh trilogy has ended with Blackout, but it hasn’t for me, not really. After 1800 pages, so much laughter, countless tears and a few frustrated screams, I know I’ll be back to reread it often. In fact, I’d already reread both Feed and Deadline more than once. Why would Blackout deserve any less? In any case, I’ve gained more from this experience than just a book I can label as my all-time favorite. I’ve bonded with people over it, and today I have the privilege of calling some of them my friends. We are a diverse group, but we started with this one thing we had in common, and in time, we developed some more. Therefore, it seems vastly unfair to call this just another trilogy. For me, it was much more than that. It was a chapter of my life and a truly life-changing experience. <br /><br />Aside from the already released <i>Countdown</i>, Mira Grant will write two more novellas in the Newslesh universe, <i>San Diego 2014: The Last Stand of the California Browncoats</i>, and <i>How Green This Land, How Blue This Sea.</i> Seanan McGuire will also launch another duology with Orbit: <i>Parasitology</i> and <i>Symbiogenesis</i>, as Mira Grant. The story will have nothing to do with the Masons, but I’m sure it will be amazing. I guess we still have something to look forward to after all.<br /><br /><b><i>We know that we were in the right<br />(The coming dawn, the ending night).<br />So here is when we stop the lies.<br />The time is come. We have to Rise.</i><br />-From <i>Dandelion Mine</i>, the blog of Magdalene Grace Garcia, August 7, 2041.</b><br /><br />Also posted at <a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nocturnal Library</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12795285213460556263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_326772233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326772233" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326772233?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13022715-blackout">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326772233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5618074652570900785">I was over the top excited to read this final installment, but I admit that I was also nervous. I loved <i>Deadline</i>, but I found myself balking a bit at what Alaric would call the “Mad Science.” I have no flipping clue how to review this and remain spoiler free but I am going to try my hardest!<br/><br/>And I guess that means that I can’t even really summarize anything that’s happened in the previous two books. Ummm… there were conspiracies and deaths (oh so many deaths!), high-stakes journalism and heroic b</span>
  <span id="freeText5618074652570900785" style="display:none">I was over the top excited to read this final installment, but I admit that I was also nervous. I loved <i>Deadline</i>, but I found myself balking a bit at what Alaric would call the “Mad Science.” I have no flipping clue how to review this and remain spoiler free but I am going to try my hardest!<br /><br />And I guess that means that I can’t even really summarize anything that’s happened in the previous two books. Ummm… there were conspiracies and deaths (oh so many deaths!), high-stakes journalism and heroic bloggers, twists that we never saw coming, and a few zombies thrown in for good measure. I laughed, I cried, I shook my fist in frustration. <br /><br />Here’s what I absolutely loved about this installment: I had so many doubts, but Mira Grant made me forget every single one. I got so swept up in the first two thirds of this book. For the first two thirds, I couldn’t care less just how out-there the science was, or how random the plot, or how convenient some of the scenarios. Grant really knows how to keep the pace moving and her characters are each so unique and full of personality. I loved the entire ensemble.<br /><br />Still… something was missing in this book for me. I just didn’t feel the emotional gut-wrench that I’d become accustomed to with the previous two books. The first two books in this series made my cry <i>real tears</i> – not just a few little prickles but full on <i>crying</i>. And, just to put things in perspective – this book has just as much death as the previous two. But no tears. Even in the climactic, endgame scene involving my favorite character – I just didn’t feel it. <br /><br />I think the forward momentum in this book really stalled out for the last third. Things started to feel repetitive: run, fight, use witty banter as a coping mechanism, describe a posh hotel in intricate detail, run, fight, use witty banter as a coping mechanism, describe a posh hospital in intricate detail, run, fight, use witty banter as a coping mechanism, describe a posh laboratory in intricate detail... and so on. And the reasoning behind all of this running felt shaky at best. The witty banter, which I previously found funny, really started to wear on me by the end. I just wanted someone to show an honest emotion! Stop joking about it for like a second! Then, feel free to resume.<br /><br />However, all of these things were more like niggling doubts I had. The major thing that prevented me from really loving this book was something very very spoilerific, so you’ll all have to excuse me if this gets really confusing.<br /><br />Remember at the end of <i>Feed?</i> When Mira Grant did one of the most courageous, bold things I’ve ever seen in fiction and just blew all of our hearts to smithereens? I felt like I actually grieved. But then, in this book… it really felt to me like all of that courage and bravery was just being undone. It felt like a <i>major</i> cop-out on her part. And I did love the scenes where she attempted to remind us all of that certain event, and that it had happened, and that it could never be changed. BUT, for all of this verbal reminding, I never felt like she showed us that it hadn’t been magically undone. If a hypothetical “development” walks, talks, and goes by the name of a duck, isn’t it essentially a duck? And I really didn’t want it to be a duck, at least not all of the time. I wanted it to have issues acting like a duck some of the time. I wanted it to forget how to quack or waddle or swim. I wanted its little duckie friends not to recognize it immediately. Otherwise, it just feels so shallow. It doesn’t feel real. It feels like a magic fairy tale solution. <br /><br />Are you all confused yet? Time to wrap this up then. In short, I still really liked this series. It’s fun; it’s fast-paced; it’s much better and more inventive than most. I had my issues with it but I think they’re more about personal preference. These books are well worth reading.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Temple of the Dog - <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NmxaFf-lpZY" rel="nofollow noopener">Say Hello to Heaven</a><br /><br />I have no idea why these books remind me of my favorite 90's grunge bands, but there it is. Of course, I used a Pearl Jam song for George and a Soundgarden song for Shaun so... the only natural thing to do for this book is Temple of the Dog. *wink*<br /><br />This song really isn't for either of them though. This was written by the remaining members of Mother Love Bone, after their lead singer Andrew Wood died. This is my song for the wall - for all the brilliant characters I mourned during the course of this series. <br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/05/adult-review-blackout-by-mira-grant.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5618074652570900785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
